⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم من الناس من زعم أن استثناء عين المقدم لا ينتج عين التالي إذا كان مقدم المتّصلة جزئيا كما في قولنا كلما كان بعض «أب» فـ «ج د»، فأما إذا قلنا لكن بعض «أب» فلا يلزم منه ج د فإنه يمكن أن يكون البعض من الألف الذي في الاستثناء غير البعض من الألف الذي كان موضوع الباء في المقدم. غير أنه فاسد وقد مرّ من الكلام فيه من قبل ولأن الكلام في استثناء المقدم ولو كان كما ذكرتم فلا يكون قولنا لكن بعض أب» استثناء عين المقدم بل استثناء شيء يمكن أن يكون عين المقدم ولا يلزم من استثناء بل هذا الشيء استثناء عين المقدم فإذن لا يلزم منه عين التالي. وبالجملة فالشرطية إذا كانت مهملة أو جزئية والمقدم في كل واحدة منهما جزئياً أو كليا : فإنه منتج يلزم من وجود الملزوم وجود اللازم، ومن عدم اللازم عدم الملزوم يمكن من اللوازم أن يقيد عند الاستثناء بقيد يفهم منه استثناء عين المقدم وهو الملزوم، أو يفهم منه استثناء نقيض التالي وهو اللازم.
Then among people is one who claimed that excepting the exact antecedent does not produce the exact consequent when the antecedent of the conditional is particular, as in our saying: 'Whenever some A is B, then C is D.' So if we say 'But some A is B,' it does not follow that C is D, because it is possible that the 'some' of the A in the exception is different from the 'some' of the A that was the subject of the B in the antecedent. However, this is corrupt, and discussion about it has passed before, and because the discussion is about excepting the antecedent, and if it were as you mentioned, then our saying 'But some A is B' is not an exception of the exact antecedent, but an exception of something that could be the exact antecedent, and an exception of this thing does not necessitate an exception of the exact antecedent, hence the exact consequent does not follow. In summary, the conditional, whether indefinite or particular, and the antecedent in each of them being particular or universal, is productive: from the existence of the necessary condition (malzum) follows the existence of the necessary (lazim), and from the non-existence of the necessary (lazim) follows the non-existence of the necessary condition (malzum). Among the necessary conditions (lawazim), it can be qualified, when excepted, by a qualification from which is understood the exception of the exact antecedent, which is the malzum, or from which is understood the exception of the contrary of the consequent, which is the lazim.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage is a correction of a mistaken view about conditional syllogisms (qiyas istithna'i muttasil). The author first presents the erroneous claim: some people assert that when the antecedent of a conditional is particular (juz'i), excepting the exact antecedent does not yield the exact consequent. They give an example: 'Whenever some A is B, then C is D' – if we except 'some A is B', it is possible the 'some' in the exception refers to a different subset than the one originally in the antecedent, so the exception is not of the exact antecedent, and thus does not produce the consequent. The author rejects this as corrupt (fasid). He argues that the discussion is about excepting the exact antecedent; if the exception is of something that could be the exact antecedent, it is not truly an exception of the exact antecedent, so it does not produce the consequent. The correct view, presented next, is that a conditional, whether indefinite (muhmala) or particular (juz'iyya), with its antecedent particular or universal, is productive. The principle is: from the existence of the necessary condition (malzum) follows the existence of the necessary (lazim), and from the non-existence of the necessary follows the non-existence of the necessary condition. The exception must be qualified to indicate that it is the exact antecedent (the malzum) or the negation of the consequent (the lazim). Thus, the productivity does not depend on universality but on the exactness of the exception. The author uses variables like 'أب' (A B) and 'ج د' (C D) as placeholders for terms, common in logical discourse.

A) Yes, because the exception is of the exact antecedent.
B) No, because the antecedent is particular.
C) Only if the exception specifies the same 'some'.
D) No, because the conditional is not universal.

Key Takeaway
A conditional syllogism is productive regardless of whether the antecedent is universal or particular, as long as the exception is of the exact antecedent (malzum) or the negation of the consequent (lazim).

Mediated Consequence in Conditional Syllogisms
Author rebuts the claim that logical consequence cannot be mediated.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how mediated logical consequence works in a conditional syllogism and defend it against the objection that consequence must be immediate.

Core Idea
Logical consequence can be mediated via a middle term without being immediate.

In this passage, the author addresses a crucial objection raised by some theologians: that a conditional syllogism with a chain of implications (A → B, B → C) cannot yield the conclusion A → C because the consequence must be immediate. The author defends the validity of mediated consequence by explaining how the middle term bridges the gap. This lesson will guide you through the objection, the author's response, and the logical mechanism using placeholder variables.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Find the theologians' claim that the first condition cannot be a necessary condition for the third without a medium. They argue that if A is a condition for B, and B for C, then A cannot directly necessitate C.
The objection denies the validity of transitive conditional chains.
2
Extract the author's response
The author replies that A is a necessary condition for C, but not in itself; it is a necessary condition when the medium (B) obtains. That is, A necessitates B, and B necessitates C, so when A obtains, B obtains, and then C obtains.
The key phrase: 'it is a necessary condition when the medium obtains, but a necessary condition when the medium obtains is not a necessary condition in itself.'
3
Analyze the variable notation
The author uses Arabic letters (أب, ج د, هز) to represent the statements in the conditional chain. 'Whenever أ ب then ج د' and 'Whenever ج د then ه ز'. The minor term (أب) is not directly a condition for the major (هز), but through the middle (ج د).
The letters are placeholders; note that 'أب' means A and B together, but here it's treated as a single antecedent.
4
Understand the extraction nuance
The author clarifies that extracting a part of the antecedent (e.g., one conjunct) does not necessarily yield the consequent unless that part's extraction entails the extraction of the whole antecedent. This refines the condition for valid istithna'.
This addresses a subtle point about conditional syllogisms with compound antecedents.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما إذا لم يكن فلا؛ وفيه من الكلام فإن من أصحاب علم الكلام من ينكر هذا ويقول: إن الأول ملزوم للثاني بلا واسطة، والثاني للثالث كذلك. ولا يمكن أن يكون الأول ملزوما للثالث بلا واسطة فيما نحن فيه؛ فكيف يكون ملزوما له. ولا يظن أن الشيء إذا كان ملزوما للشيء بواسطة شيء آخر كان ملزوما له حتى لا يمكن وجوده بدونه من حيث هو هو. نعم إنه ملزوم عند تحقق الواسطة لكن الملزوم عند تحقق الواسطة لا يكون ملزوما من حيث هو هو. وقد علمت بأن جزء الملزوم لا يلزم أن يكون ملزوما. وإن قيل إنه إذا لم يكن ملزوما للثالث كان من الممكن أن يكون بدون الثالث؛ وحينئذ يلزم أن لا يكون ملزوما للثاني أو الثاني لا يكون ملزوما للثالث. والكل باطل؛ إذ الكلام في كونه ملزوما فنقول الجواب عنه قد مر: فإنه وإن لم يكن ملزوما بلا واسطة شيء فقد كان ملزوما عند تحقق ذلك الشيء. وإن قيل لو كان كما ذكرتم لكان قولنا كلما كان "أب" فـ "ج د"، وكلما كان "ج د" فـ "هز" عقيما لا ينتج: فإنه لا يلزم منه قولنا كلما كان "أب" فـ "هز" فنقول إنه لا ينتج من حيث هو هو بل ينتج باعتبار أن الأوسط يتحقق عند تحقق الأصغر لا محالة. فالأصغر وهو "أب" لا يكون مستلزما للأكبر وهو "هز" من حيث هو هو بل يكون مستلزما من حيث إنه يكون مستلزما للأوسط. ولو كان كذلك فلا يمكن أن يتحقق بدون الأوسط بل إذا تحقق تحقق مع الأوسط، ولا يمكن أن يتحقق الأصغر بدون الأكبر؛ فيلزم أن يتحقق الأكبر. إذن فقولنا لا يلزم من استثناء البعض من أجزاء المقدم عين التالي هو أنه لا يلزم من استثنائه وهو جزء من أجزاء المقدم من حيث هو جزء من أجزائها لا من حيث إنه من جملة ما يلزم من استثنائه استثناء عين المقدم. واعلم بأن هذا القياس من جملة ما يورد عليه من الشبه؛ وذلك بوجوه:
As for when it is not, then not; and therein is discussion. For among the theologians there are those who deny this and say: The first is a necessary condition for the second without a medium, and the second for the third likewise. And it is not possible that the first be a necessary condition for the third without a medium in our subject; so how could it be a necessary condition for it? And do not think that if something is a necessary condition for something else through the medium of another thing, it is a necessary condition for it such that it cannot exist without it in itself. Yes, it is a necessary condition when the medium obtains, but a necessary condition when the medium obtains is not a necessary condition in itself. And you have known that a part of the necessary condition is not necessarily a necessary condition. And if it is said: If it is not a necessary condition for the third, then it is possible that it exist without the third; and then it follows that it is not a necessary condition for the second, or the second is not a necessary condition for the third. All of this is false, because the discussion is about its being a necessary condition. So we say: The answer to it has passed: for even if it was not a necessary condition without a medium for something, it was a necessary condition when that medium obtains. And if it is said: If it were as you mentioned, then our statement 'Whenever A is B, then C is D' and 'Whenever C is D, then E is Z' would be sterile, yielding nothing; for it does not follow from it our statement 'Whenever A is B, then E is Z'. So we say: It does not produce from itself, but it produces by considering that the middle term obtains upon the obtaining of the minor term without fail. So the minor term, which is A B, is not a necessary condition for the major term, which is E Z, in itself, but it is a necessary condition in that it is a necessary condition for the middle term. And if that is the case, then it cannot exist without the middle term; rather, if it exists, it exists with the middle term, and the minor term cannot exist without the major; therefore the major must exist. So our statement 'It does not follow from extracting a part of the parts of the antecedent the identical consequent' means that it does not follow from extracting it (a part of the parts of the antecedent) in that it is a part of its parts, not in that it is among that whose extraction necessitates extracting the identical antecedent. And know that this syllogism is among what objections are raised against it; and that in aspects:
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage is a critical defense of the conditional syllogism (qiyas istithna'i) against an objection from theologians. The author addresses the claim that a logical consequence cannot be mediated. The objection states that if A is a necessary condition for B, and B for C, then A cannot be a necessary condition for C directly, so the conditional chain fails. The author replies that A is a necessary condition for C indirectly, via the medium B. It is not a necessary condition in itself (in and of itself), but it is a necessary condition when the medium exists. This is like the syllogism: 'If it is night, then the moon is visible' and 'If the moon is visible, then the world is illuminated.' The conclusion 'If it is night, then the world is illuminated' is valid because the middle term (the moon being visible) mediates. The author uses placeholder letters (أب, ج د, هز) to illustrate: when the minor term (أب) obtains, the middle (ج د) obtains, and then the major (هز) obtains. The minor is not directly necessary for the major, but through the middle. The passage also clarifies that extracting a part of the antecedent (like a conjunct) does not necessarily yield the consequent, but if that part is such that its extraction entails the extraction of the whole antecedent, then it does. The author concludes by noting that this syllogism is subject to objections, which will be discussed.

Checkpoint
In the chain 'If the prayer is invalid (A), then the wudu' is broken (B); if the wudu' is broken (B), then the person is impure (C)', does A directly necessitate C?
A) Yes, because the chain is transitive.
B) No, because A only necessitates C through B.
C) Yes, because A and C are logically equivalent.
D) No, because there is no connection.

Key Takeaway
Logical consequence can be mediated through a middle term; the validity of a conditional chain depends on the necessary obtainment of the medium.

Construct a conditional syllogism with two premises (A → B, B → C) using an Islamic legal example (e.g., drinking nabidh leads to intoxication, intoxication leads to prohibition). Explain why the conclusion A → C is valid through mediation.

Understanding the First Objection Against Conditional Syllogism
Author presents the first objection against conditional syllogism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the two-case objection against conditional syllogism and identify the logical mistake in the objector's reasoning.

Core Idea
The objector mistakes the conditional's necessity for redundancy.

The conditional syllogism (qiyas istithna'i) is a cornerstone of Islamic logic. However, it has been challenged by an objection that claims it can never yield new knowledge. This objection argues that the syllogism is only productive in two impossible scenarios. In this lesson, we will unpack this objection to understand its logical structure, preparing to evaluate its validity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two productive scenarios
The objector says the syllogism is only productive when the necessary condition (antecedent) is true (modus ponens) or when the consequent is false (modus tollens). Note this classification.
These are the only two forms of conditional syllogism according to the objector.
2
Examine the first scenario (modus ponens)
The objector claims that in modus ponens, the conditional already necessitates the consequent, so inferring it is redundant. He argues that if the conditional implies the consequent, then its absence would follow from the absence of the consequent, but that does not allow inferring the absence of the antecedent.
The objector uses a modus tollens-like reasoning to argue against modus ponens.
3
Examine the second scenario (modus tollens)
Similarly, in modus tollens, the objector claims that the conditional necessitates the negation of the antecedent, so inferring it is redundant. He argues that if the conditional's negation follows from the existence of the antecedent, then from the existence of the antecedent the consequent does not follow.
The objector attempts to show that both forms lead to impossibility.
4
Identify the objector's hidden assumption
The objector assumes that because the conditional itself is a necessary concomitant (mulazama), it cannot be used to produce new knowledge. He fails to see that the syllogism combines the conditional with an additional premise to derive a conclusion not contained in the conditional alone.
This assumption is the weak point that the author will later refute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
منها أنه لا يكون منتجا إلا في صورة يكون الملزوم متحققا، أو في صورة يكون اللازم منتفيًا؛ وذلك لأن المطلوب إما عين اللازم أو نقيض الملزوم. وكونه منتجا في الصورة الأولى محال؛ إذ الملازمة فيها مستلزمة لوجود اللازم؛ وحينئذ يلزم أن يكون انتفاؤها من لوازم انتفاء اللازم. ولو كان كذلك فلا يلزم من انتفاء اللازم انتفاء الملزوم؛ وقد كانت الملازمة من اللوازم على ما عرف. وكذلك في الصورة الثانية فإن الملازمة فيها مستلزمة لعدم الملزوم؛ وحينئذ يلزم أن يكون انتفاؤها من لوازم وجود الملزوم. ولو كان كذلك فلا يلزم من وجود الملزوم وجود اللازم كذلك فإن من المحال أن يلزم من وجوده وجود اللازم؛ ولا ملازمة بينه وبين ذلك.
Among them: That it is not productive except in the case where the necessary condition is realized, or in the case where the consequent is negated; because the required is either the identical consequent or the contradictory of the necessary condition. And its being productive in the first case is impossible; for the conditional implication in it necessitates the existence of the consequent; and then it follows that its absence is among the necessary concomitants of the absence of the consequent. And if that were the case, then from the absence of the consequent the absence of the necessary condition does not follow; while the conditional implication was among the necessary concomitants, as is known. And similarly in the second case, for the conditional implication in it necessitates the non-existence of the necessary condition; and then it follows that its absence is among the necessary concomitants of the existence of the necessary condition. And if that were the case, then from the existence of the necessary condition the existence of the consequent does not follow; likewise, for it is impossible that from its existence follows the existence of the consequent; and there is no implication between them.
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage presents the first objection against the conditional syllogism. The objector claims that the conditional syllogism (qiyas istithna'i) is only productive in two impossible scenarios: either when the necessary condition (malzum - antecedent or required) is actual, or when the consequent (lazim) is negated. The objection argues that in the first case (modus ponens: if A then B, and A is true, therefore B is true), the conditional itself presupposes the existence of the consequent, so inferring the consequent is redundant and impossible to be 'productive' of new knowledge. Moreover, the objector claims that from the absence of the consequent, the absence of the antecedent does not follow (modus tollens would be invalid). In the second case (modus tollens: if A then B, and B is false, therefore A is false), the objection states that the conditional necessarily requires the absence of the antecedent, so inferring that absence from the absence of the consequent is again redundant. The author presents this objection to refute it later, but in this passage he is simply stating it. The key point is that the objector misunderstands the nature of conditional implication, thinking that the conditional itself being a necessary concomitant prevents valid inference. In reality, the conditional syllogism is productive because it combines the conditional premise with an additional statement to derive a new conclusion. For example: 'If the prayer is valid, then the wudu' is valid. The prayer is valid. Therefore the wudu' is valid.' This is productive because the second premise is not contained in the first.

Key Terms

لازم
ملازمة

B) The antecedent is always false.
C) The conditional implies its own truth.
D) The syllogism is invalid in all figures.

Key Takeaway
The objection against conditional syllogism argues it is redundant, but this misunderstands how the syllogism combines the conditional with an additional premise to produce new knowledge.

Refuting the Objection to Conditional Syllogisms
Author refutes objection that extracting the antecedent is insufficient to yield the consequent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the logical error in the objection that affirming the antecedent does not produce the consequent in conditional syllogisms.

Core Idea
The objection confuses the necessity of the conditional with the validity of modus ponens and modus tollens.

Islamic logicians faced objections to the foundational forms of conditional reasoning. This passage presents one such objection: that affirming the antecedent (istithna' 'ayn al-muqaddam) cannot be productive of the consequent. Understanding this objection and its flaw sharpens your ability to defend logical inference in Islamic sciences like usul al-fiqh and kalam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Objection's Claim
Read the passage and locate the objector's main claim: 'Extracting the identical antecedent cannot be productive of the identical consequent.' This attacks modus ponens.
The objector tries to show that if modus ponens were valid, it would lead to a contradiction.
2
Trace the Objector's Reasoning
The objector argues: if affirming the antecedent is productive, it must be either by virtue of the antecedent being a necessary condition for the consequent or not. If not, it's impossible. If yes, then denying the consequent (modus tollens) would also be productive by that same virtue, which the objector claims is false.
This reasoning attempts to create a dilemma that undermines modus ponens.
3
Spot the Logical Error
The error is that the objector assumes modus tollens is unproductive, but in standard logic it is valid. The objector's argument incorrectly concludes that modus ponens leads to a problem; in fact, both forms are productive and consistent.
The fallacy is a false dichotomy or a confusion about the nature of necessary condition.
4
Apply the Correct Islamic Logical Form
Recall the valid forms: modus ponens (If A then B, A, therefore B) and modus tollens (If A then B, not B, therefore not A). Both are productive qiyas istithna'i. The objection does not refute them.
Use a fiqh example to see the validity: 'If nabidh is intoxicating, it is forbidden. It is intoxicating. Therefore it is forbidden.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها أن يقال: إن استثناء عين المقدم لا يمكن أن يكون منتجا عين التالي؛ فإنه إذا كان منتجا فإما أن يكون منتجا بوصف كونه مستلزما للتالي أو لا يكون فإن لم يكن فظاهر لاستحالة أن يكون منتجا لا بوصف كونه مستلزما لذلك. وإن كان فكذلك؛ فإن استثناء نقيض التالي حينئذ لا يكون منتجا نقيض المقدم بل يكون منتجا نقيض المقدم بوصف كونه مستلزما. ولا يلزم من نقيض هذا المجموع نقيض المقدم. ولا يقال بل يلزم فإن اتصاف المقدم بوصف كونه مستلزما متحقق فلا يمكن أن يكون انتفاء المجموع بانتفائه؛ إذ الاتصاف متحقق في نفس الأمر لا على تقدير انتفاء لازم من لوازم المجموع
And among them: That it is said: Extracting the identical antecedent cannot be productive of the identical consequent; for if it is productive, it is either productive by virtue of being a necessary condition for the consequent or not. If it is not, then it is obvious that it is impossible that it be productive without being a necessary condition for that. And if it is [productive by that virtue], then similarly; for extracting the contradictory of the consequent then is not productive of the contradictory of the antecedent, but rather is productive of the contradictory of the antecedent by virtue of being a necessary condition. And the contradictory of this whole does not follow from the contradictory of the antecedent. And it is not said that it does follow, for the characterization of the antecedent by virtue of being a necessary condition is realized; so it is not possible that the absence of the whole occurs by its absence; because the characterization is realized in actuality, not upon the supposition of the absence of a necessary concomitant of the whole.
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage presents the second objection to the conditional syllogism. The objector argues that affirming the antecedent (extracting the identical antecedent) cannot be productive of the consequent. The reasoning is that if the antecedent is a necessary condition for the consequent (i.e., if A then B), then affirming A should produce B. But the objector claims that if A is a necessary condition for B, then denying B should produce not-A (modus tollens). However, the objector says that this is not the case: from the negation of B, we get the negation of A only by virtue of A being a necessary condition for B, but that this is not a productive inference because the characterization of A as a necessary condition for B is already known. Moreover, the objector argues that from the negation of the whole (i.e., the negation of the conditional plus the antecedent?)... The passage is dense, but the gist is that the objector claims this leads to a paradox or inconsistency. The author will refute this later, but here he is presenting the objection. In standard logic, the objection is invalid because modus ponens and modus tollens are both valid and productive; the conditional syllogism is not circular. For example: 'If the meat is not slaughtered according to Sharia, then it is not permissible to eat. The meat is not slaughtered according to Sharia. Therefore it is not permissible to eat.' This is productive because you combine two separate premises.

استثناء نقيض التالي

Key Takeaway
The objection's flaw is assuming modus tollens is unproductive; both modus ponens and modus tollens are valid and productive in conditional syllogisms.

Third Objection: Conditional Syllogism Leads to Contradiction
Author presents third objection that conditional syllogism is self-contradictory.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a false dilemma objection to the conditional syllogism and distinguish valid from invalid reasoning in conditional arguments using Islamic examples.

Core Idea
The third objection falsely claims modus ponens and modus tollens cannot coexist; they are two valid forms of the same conditional.

In this passage, the author presents a third objection against the conditional syllogism (qiyas istithna'i). The objector argues that if modus ponens is valid, then modus tollens must be invalid, and vice versa. This objection is a false dilemma that misunderstands the nature of conditional implications. We will analyze the structure of this objection to learn how to recognize similar fallacies in theological and juristic debates.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conditional syllogism forms
Modus ponens extracts the antecedent to yield the consequent; modus tollens extracts the contradictory of the consequent to yield the contradictory of the antecedent.
2
Understand the objector's false dilemma
The objector claims that if modus ponens is productive, then either the antecedent is incompatible with the conditional (making modus ponens invalid) or it is not (making modus tollens invalid). This presents a false choice.
3
Test with an Islamic example
Consider: 'If the witness is truthful, then his testimony is accepted.' Both forms are valid: affirming truthfulness leads to acceptance (modus ponens); denying acceptance leads to denying truthfulness (modus tollens).
4
Recognize the logical error
The objector assumes that the antecedent being incompatible with the conditional is the only way to preserve consistency. In reality, the conditional itself ensures both forms are valid; they do not conflict.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها أن يقال: استثناء عين المقدم إذا كان منتجا عين التالي فاستثناء نقيض التالي لا يكون منتجا نقيض المقدم. فإنه إذا كان منتجا فلا يخلو من أن يكون استثناء عين المقدم منافيا للملازمة بينهما; وحينئذ يلزم أن لا يكون استثناء عين المقدم مستلزما عين التالي البتة. فإن من المحال أن يكون مستلزما؛ ولا ملازمة بينهما، أو لا يكون منافيا؛ وحينئذ يلزم أن لا يكون استثناء نقيض التالي مستلزما نقيض
And among them: That it is said: If extracting the identical antecedent is productive of the identical consequent, then extracting the contradictory of the consequent is not productive of the contradictory of the antecedent. For if it is productive, then either extracting the identical antecedent is incompatible with the conditional implication between them; and then it would follow that extracting the identical antecedent does not necessitate the identical consequent at all. For it is impossible that it be necessary; and there is no conditional implication between them. Or it is not incompatible; and then it would follow that extracting the contradictory of the consequent does not necessitate the contradictory
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage presents the third objection against the conditional syllogism. The objector argues that if modus ponens (affirming the antecedent to get the consequent) is valid, then modus tollens (denying the consequent to get the denial of the antecedent) must be invalid, and vice versa. The reasoning is that if the conditional 'if A then B' holds, then either A is incompatible with the conditional (which would make modus ponens invalid) or not. If A is incompatible with the conditional, then affirming A would contradict the conditional, so modus ponens fails. If A is not incompatible, then the conditional is consistent with A, but then denying B would not lead to denying A because the conditional does not require A to be the sole sufficient condition. This objection is a false dilemma. In fact, both modus ponens and modus tollens are valid forms for the same conditional. For example: 'If the witness is truthful, then his testimony is accepted. The witness is truthful. Therefore his testimony is accepted.' (modus ponens) and 'If the witness is truthful, then his testimony is accepted. The witness's testimony is not accepted. Therefore the witness is not truthful.' (modus tollens) are both valid and consistent. The text cuts off before presenting the full refutation, but the objection itself is clear.

Key Terms
منافي
ملازمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
The third objection claims that if modus ponens is valid, then modus tollens must be invalid. Which Islamic example demonstrates both are valid?
A) If the prayer is valid, then wudu' is valid. Wudu' is valid, so prayer is valid.
B) If the prayer is valid, then wudu' is valid. Prayer is valid, so wudu' is valid. (modus ponens) and If wudu' is invalid, then prayer is invalid. (modus tollens)
C) If the sun rises, then it is day. It is day, so the sun rose.
D) If the moon is eclipsed, then night is dark. Night is not dark, so moon is not eclipsed.

Key Takeaway
The third objection against conditional syllogism is a false dilemma; both modus ponens and modus tollens are valid forms of the same conditional argument.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The sale is valid, so ownership transfers.' Then: 'If the sale is valid, then ownership transfers. Ownership does not transfer, so the sale is invalid.' Both are valid.

The Productivity of Conditional Syllogisms: Objection and Answer
Author presents an objection and its answer on conditional syllogisms.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the objection to conditional syllogisms and explain how mental assent (taslim dhihni) resolves the dialectical challenge.

Core Idea
A syllogism's validity in debate depends on mental assent, not external truth.

In this passage, the author engages with a sophisticated objection against the productivity of conditional syllogisms (qiyas istithna'i). The objector argues that in both standard forms – affirming the antecedent or denying the consequent – the syllogism is circular and does not yield new knowledge. The author's answer hinges on a crucial distinction between actual truth and mental acceptance, a cornerstone of dialectical logic (jadal).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two images of conditional syllogisms
The objection targets two forms: (1) when the antecedent (malzum) is affirmed, and (2) when the consequent (lazim) is negated. Locate these in the passage and note how the objector frames them.
These correspond to modus ponens and modus tollens in Aristotelian logic.
2
Extract the objector's argument for the first image
In the first image, the objector claims: the conditional relation (mulazama) entails the consequent's existence; so negating the relation depends on negating the consequent. But from negating the consequent, negating the antecedent does not follow, so the syllogism is invalid.
This is an attack on modus ponens as not productive.
3
Extract the objector's argument for the second image
Similarly, in the second image, the conditional relation entails the antecedent's non-existence; so negating the relation depends on the antecedent's existence. But from the antecedent's existence, the consequent's existence does not follow, so the syllogism fails.
This is an attack on modus tollens.
4
Understand the author's key distinction: truth vs. mental assent
The author replies that productivity does not require actual truth of the conditional and its parts, but only mental assent (taslim dhihni) – the interlocutor's acceptance of them. This shifts the ground from ontological necessity to dialectical context.
Mental assent may or may not align with reality; it is a negotiated agreement for the sake of argument.
5
Analyze the author's rebuttal of the first image
The author denies that the conditional relation alone entails the consequent; rather, the conditional relation together with the antecedent entails the consequent. Thus, if the consequent is negated and the conditional relation is still mentally accepted, the antecedent is negated by the necessity of negating the whole (antecedent + conditional).
This preserves the validity of modus ponens under mental assent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
منها أنه لا يكون منتجا إلا في صورة يكون الملزوم متحققا، أو في صورة يكون اللازم منتفيًا؛ وذلك لأن المطلوب إما عين اللازم أو نقيض الملزوم. وكونه منتجا في الصورة الأولى محال؛ إذ الملازمة فيها مستلزمة لوجود اللازم؛ وحينئذ يلزم أن يكون انتفاؤها من لوازم انتفاء اللازم. ولو كان كذلك فلا يلزم من انتفاء اللازم انتفاء الملزوم؛ وقد كانت الملازمة من اللوازم على ما عرف. وكذلك في الصورة الثانية فإن الملازمة فيها مستلزمة لعدم الملزوم؛ وحينئذ يلزم أن يكون انتفاؤها من لوازم وجود الملزوم. ولو كان كذلك فلا يلزم من وجود الملزوم وجود اللازم كذلك فإن من المحال أن يلزم من وجوده وجود اللازم؛ ولا ملازمة بينه وبين ذلك.

أما الجواب فنقول في الأول منها: إنه من جملة ما قد مر الكلام فيه؛ وذلك لأن كونه منتجا لا يفتقر إلى صدق الشرطية وصدق أجزائها في نفس الأمر بل يفتقر إلى التسليم الذهني صدقها وصدق المقدم منها أو صدق نقيض التالي كذلك. والتسليم الذهني قد يكون مطابقا لما يكون في الخارج، وقد لا يكون. وأما قوله إن الملازمة في الصورة الأولى مستلزمة لوجود اللازم، فذلك في حيز المنع بل الملازمة مع تحقق الملزوم مما يستلزم وجود اللازم فيها. وإن قيل هب أنه كذلك لكن لا يلزم من انتفاء اللازم انتفاء الملزوم حينئذ فنقول بل يلزم فإن انتفاء اللازم من جملة ما تحقق الملازمة بينهما وإلا لا يكون ذلك الانتفاء انتفاء اللازم. ولما كانت الملازمة متحققة عند ذلك الانتفاء كان الملزوم منتفيًا بالضرورة ضرورة انتفاء المجموع وهو الملزوم مع الملازمة. وعلى هذا في الصورة الباقية.
Among them is that it is not productive except in a form where the antecedent is true, or in a form where the consequent is negated; because the demand is either the very consequent or the negation of the antecedent. Its being productive in the first form is impossible; since the conditional relation therein entails the existence of the consequent; and therefore it follows that its negation is among the necessary consequences of the negation of the consequent. But if it were so, then from the negation of the consequent the negation of the antecedent does not follow; and the conditional relation was among the necessary consequences as was known. Similarly in the second form: the conditional relation therein entails the non-existence of the antecedent; and thus it follows that its negation is among the necessary consequences of the existence of the antecedent. And if it were so, then from the existence of the antecedent the existence of the consequent does not follow; for it is impossible that from its existence the existence of the consequent follows; and there is no conditional relation between them.

As for the answer, we say regarding the first of them: it is among what has been discussed before; because its being productive does not depend on the truth of the conditional statement and the truth of its parts in themselves, but rather depends on mental assent to their truth and the truth of the antecedent from it or the truth of the negation of the consequent likewise. And mental assent may correspond to what is in external reality, and may not. As for his statement that the conditional relation in the first form entails the existence of the consequent, that is subject to denial; rather the conditional relation, given the existence of the antecedent, is what entails the existence of the consequent in it. And if it is said: suppose it is so, but from the negation of the consequent the negation of the antecedent does not follow then, we say: rather it does follow, for the negation of the consequent is among what the conditional relation is realized between them, otherwise that negation would not be negation of the consequent. And since the conditional relation is realized at that negation, the antecedent is negated necessarily, by the necessity of the negation of the whole, which is the antecedent together with the conditional relation. And similarly for the remaining form.
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage presents an objection to the productivity of conditional syllogisms (qiyas istithna'i) in the two standard images: when the antecedent (ملزوم) is true (first image) or when the consequent (لازم) is negated (second image). The objector argues that in the first image, the conditional relation itself entails the consequent's existence, so negating the relation (i.e., the conditional) would depend on the negation of the consequent, but from the negation of the consequent the negation of the antecedent does not necessarily follow, so the syllogism is not productive. Similarly in the second image: the conditional relation entails the antecedent's non-existence, so its negation would depend on the antecedent's existence, but from the antecedent's existence the consequent's existence does not necessarily follow. Thus the objector claims both images fail.

The author answers by distinguishing between external truth and mental assent (taslim dhihni). The productivity of the syllogism depends not on the actual truth of the conditional and its parts, but on the interlocutor's mental acceptance of them. Therefore, even if the conditional relation entails the existence of the consequent given the antecedent, the objection's inference is denied. In the first image, the conditional together with the antecedent does necessitate the consequent; but the objection confuses the entailment of the conditional with the entailment from the negation of the consequent. The author adds that if the consequent is negated and the conditional relation is still mentally accepted, then the antecedent is necessarily negated by the negation of the whole (the antecedent plus the conditional). The same reasoning applies to the second image.

Key Terms
ملزوم
لازم
ملازمة
التسليم الذهني

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, what does the productivity of conditional syllogisms in dialectical contexts depend on?
A) The actual truth of the conditional statement
B) The mental assent (taslim dhihni) of the interlocutor
C) The existence of the antecedent in reality
D) The necessity of the consequent

Key Takeaway
The productivity of conditional syllogisms in dialectical reasoning hinges on mental assent (taslim dhihni), not external truth; the objection is rebutted by clarifying that the conditional relation together with the antecedent (or denial of consequent) entails the conclusion under mental agreement.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Task 1: In a debate about the permissibility of a new contract type, one debater says: 'If this contract involves gharar (excessive uncertainty), then it is impermissible. This contract involves gharar. Therefore it is impermissible.' The opponent objects: 'But the conditional relation itself entails the impermissibility, so your syllogism is circular.' Using the author's distinction, formulate the response that the syllogism is valid under mental assent.

Defending Conditional Syllogisms Against Three Objections
Author refutes three objections about the productivity of conditional syllogisms.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the three objections to conditional syllogisms and evaluate the author's defense using the concept of mental acceptance (taslim dhihni).

Core Idea
Conditional syllogisms work by mental acceptance, not external truth.

In this passage, the author anticipates and refutes three objections that challenge the productivity (intaj) of conditional syllogisms. Understanding these objections and their responses deepens your grasp of how conditional reasoning functions in Islamic logic. Pay attention to the key distinction between external truth and mental acceptance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three objection targets
The passage presents three objections. Look for markers (first, second, third) in the translation. The first objection claims that if the antecedent is necessary, affirming it contradicts the implication. The second objection claims that if the consequent is more general, the syllogism cannot be productive. The third objection claims that affirming the antecedent is contradictory to the implication.
2
Analyze the first objection and its answer
The author argues that productivity does not require the conditional to be factually true; mental acceptance suffices. Notice how he distinguishes between the implication alone and the implication together with the implicated.
3
Analyze the second objection and its answer
The author distinguishes between the absence of the implicated (the antecedent with the attribute of implying) and the absence of the essence itself. This subtle point defends the syllogism's validity even when the consequent is more general.
4
Analyze the third objection and its answer
The author shows that affirming the antecedent does not contradict the implication; rather, the implication is already present. The exception of the negation of the consequent remains productive.
5
Synthesize the role of mental acceptance
Across all answers, the key concept is taslim dhihni (mental acceptance). Understand that logical validity in conditional syllogisms operates in the mind, not necessarily in external reality.

المقدم. فإنه إذا كان مستلزما كان استثناء عين المقدم منافيًا للملازمة بينهما لما أن نقيض المقدم من لوازم الملازمة بينهما في هذه الصورة وهي صورة انتفاء اللازم. فيكون نقيض الملازمة من لوازم عين المقدم بالضرورة؛ وحينئذ يلزم منافيا. ث ومنها أن يقال: إذا كان التالي أعم من المقدم في التحقق فلا يمكن أن يكون منتجا لا هذا الاستثناء، ولا ذلك فإنه إذا كان منتجا فلا يخلو من أن يكون الافتراق ممكناً بين المقدم والتالي في الجملة؛ وحينئذ لا يمكن أن يكون منتجا لا هذا ولا ذلك فإنه يمكن أن يكون الافتراق متحققا بينهما حال استثناء هذا أو ذلك؛ وذلك من جملة ما ينافي القطع بكونه مستلزما، أو لا يكون ممكنا؛ وحينئذ يلزم أن لا يكون التالي أعم من المقدم في التحقق البتة. ولما لم يكن أعم منه فلا يمكن أن يكون الاستثناء منتجا وهو أعم منه حال الاستثناء. أما الجواب [1] فنقول في الأول منها: إنه من جملة ما قد مر الكلام فيه؛ وذلك لأن كونه منتجا لا يفتقر إلى صدق الشرطية وصدق أجزائها في نفس الأمر بل يفتقر إلى التسليم الذهني صدقها وصدق المقدم منها أو صدق نقيض التالي كذلك. والتسليم الذهني قد يكون مطابقا لما يكون في الخارج، وقد لا يكون. وأما قوله إن الملازمة في الصورة الأولى مستلزمة لوجود اللازم، فذلك في حيز المنع بل الملازمة مع تحقق الملزوم مما يستلزم وجود اللازم فيها. وإن قيل هب أنه كذلك لكن لا يلزم من انتفاء اللازم انتفاء الملزوم حينئذ فنقول بل يلزم فإن انتفاء اللازم من جملة ما تحقق الملازمة بينهما وإلا لا يكون ذلك الانتفاء انتفاء اللازم. ولما كانت الملازمة متحققة عند ذلك الانتفاء كان الملزوم منتفيًا بالضرورة ضرورة انتفاء المجموع وهو الملزوم مع الملازمة. وعلى هذا في الصورة الباقية. ب وفي الثاني نقول: إنه من جملة ما قد مرّ الكلام فيه أيضًا وهو أنه يلزم من انتفاء اللازم انتفاء الملزوم لا انتفاء ما يعرض له الملزومية وهو نفس الماهية من حيث هي نفس الماهية؛ فالمقدم إذن لا يكون مقدما إلا وأن يكون متصفّا بوصف كونه مستلزما للتالي، والتالي أيضًا لا يكون تاليا إلا وأن يكون متصفًا بوصف كونه لازما للمقدم. ولو كان كذلك لكان انتفاء اللازم مما يستلزم انتفاء الملزوم وهو المقدم بوصف كونه مستلزما. ولا يقال لو كان كما ذكرتم لكان الملزوم عبارة عن مجموع ذات الشيء وصفته فلا يمكن أن يكون شيئًا مفردًا البتة؛ إذ لفظ الملزوم عبارة عن شيء له الملزومية فلا يمكن أن يكون مفردًا وهو نفس ماهية الشيء لا غير. والكلام في انتفاء الملزوم بنفي اللازم لا في انتفاء تلك الماهية من حيث تلك الماهية. وإن قيل ملزومية الشيء عارضة للشيء فتكون خارجة عن ماهية الشيء وهو الملزوم. ولو كان كما ذكرتم كانت داخلة في الماهية فنقول إنها عارضة للشيء الذي هو الملزوم لا للملزوم فيكون داخلة في ماهية الملزوم لا في ماهية الشيء؛ والشيء من حيث هو الشيء لا يكون ملزوما، ولا يكون لازما بل لا يكون متصفّا بصفة أصلا . ت وفي الثالث نقول: إن الشيء إذا كان منافيًا للشيء لا يمكن أن يكون متصفّا به لاستحالة اتصافه بما ينافيه. وإنه يمكن أن يكون مع الصفة ولا يمكن أن يكون مع ما ينافيه البتة، ولو كان كذلك فلا يمكن أن يكون استثناء عين المقدم منافيًا للملازمة بينه وبين التالي. وكيف وإنه لا يمكن أن يكون ملزوما إلا وأن يكون الملازمة متحققة بينهما فإذن لا يمكن أن يكون منافيًا للملازمة. ولا يلزم من عدم كونه منافيًا للملازمة أن لا يكون استثناء نقيض التالي مستلزما نقيض المقدم بل يكون مستلزما وإلا لا يكون ذلك الاستثناء استثناء نقيض التالي. وأما قوله إنه إذا كان مستلزما كان استثناء عين المقدم منافيًا للملازمة بينهما لما أن نقيض المقدم من لوازم
The antecedent: For if it is necessary, then the exception of the very antecedent is contradictory to the implication between them because the negation of the antecedent is among the concomitants of the implication between them in this form, which is the form of the absence of the consequent. Then the negation of the implication is among the concomitants of the very antecedent necessarily; and then a contradiction follows. [Th] And among them is that it is said: If the consequent is more general than the antecedent in actuality, then it cannot be productive, neither this exception nor that. For if it were productive, it would not be free from the possibility of separation between the antecedent and consequent in general; and then it cannot be productive, neither this nor that, because it is possible that separation occurs between them at the time of excepting this or that. And that is among the things that contradict the certainty of its being necessary, or it is not possible; and then it follows that the consequent is not more general than the antecedent in actuality at all. And since it is not more general, the exception cannot be productive while it is more general than it at the time of exception. As for the answer [1], we say regarding the first of them: It is among what has already been discussed; that is because its being productive does not depend on the truth of the conditional and the truth of its parts in actual fact, but rather it depends on mental acceptance of its truth and the truth of its antecedent or the truth of the negation of its consequent likewise. Mental acceptance may correspond to what is in external reality, or it may not. As for his saying that the implication in the first form necessitates the existence of the consequent, that is subject to denial; rather, the implication together with the realization of the implicated necessitates the existence of the consequent in it. And if it is said: Grant that it is so, but the absence of the consequent does not necessitate the absence of the implicated at that time, then we say: Rather it does necessitate, for the absence of the consequent is among the things that realize the implication between them, otherwise that absence would not be the absence of the consequent. And since the implication is realized at that absence, the implicated is necessarily absent due to the necessity of the absence of the totality, which is the implicated together with the implication. And this applies to the remaining forms. [B] And regarding the second, we say: It is among what has already been discussed as well, namely that the absence of the consequent necessitates the absence of the implicated, not the absence of what has the property of being implicated, which is the essence itself considered as the essence itself. So the antecedent is not an antecedent except by being qualified by the attribute of implying the consequent, and the consequent is not a consequent except by being qualified by the attribute of being implied by the antecedent. And if it were so, then the absence of the consequent would necessitate the absence of the implicated, which is the antecedent with the attribute of implying. And it is not said: If it were as you mentioned, then the implicated would be a composite of the thing's essence and its attribute, so it cannot be a single thing at all; for the term 'implicated' refers to a thing that has implication; therefore it cannot be single, being nothing other than the thing's essence itself. And the discussion concerns the absence of the implicated by the negation of the consequent, not the absence of that essence considered as that essence. And if it is said: The implication of a thing is accidental to the thing, so it is external to the essence of the thing which is the implicated. And if it were as you said, it would be internal to the essence; we say: It is accidental to the thing which is the implicated, not to the implicated, so it is internal to the essence of the implicated, not to the essence of the thing; and the thing considered as a thing is neither implicated nor implicative, nor is it qualified by any attribute at all. [T] And regarding the third, we say: If a thing is contradictory to a thing, it cannot be qualified by it because it is impossible for it to be qualified by what contradicts it. And it can be with the attribute but cannot be with what contradicts it at all. And if it were so, then the exception of the very antecedent cannot be contradictory to the implication between it and the consequent. How so? And it cannot be implicated except while the implication is realized between them; therefore, it cannot be contradictory to the implication. And from the fact that it is not contradictory to the implication, it does not follow that the exception of the negation of the consequent does not necessitate the negation of the antecedent; rather, it does necessitate it, otherwise that exception would not be an exception of the negation of the consequent. And as for his saying: If it is necessary, then the exception of the very antecedent is contradictory to the implication between them because the negation of the antecedent is among the concomitants...
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage addresses three objections to the productivity of conditional syllogisms (qiyas istithna'i) and provides answers. The first objection concerns the case where the antecedent necessitates the consequent: if the antecedent is necessary, then affirming the antecedent seems contradictory to the implication because the negation of the antecedent is a concomitant of the implication. The answer clarifies that productivity depends on mental acceptance (taslim dhihni), not external truth. The conditional need not be true in reality; what matters is that the thinker accepts it as true. The implication together with the realization of the implicated necessitates the consequent, but the absence of the consequent necessitates the absence of the implicated (i.e., the antecedent with its attribute of implying). The second objection deals with the case where the consequent is more general than the antecedent. If the consequent is more general, then affirming the antecedent or negating the consequent may not be productive because separation is possible. The answer distinguishes between the absence of the implicated (the antecedent with the attribute of implying) and the absence of the thing's essence. The antecedent's being a 'muqaddam' is tied to its attribute of implying; thus, negation of the consequent negates the antecedent only insofar as it has that attribute, not its bare essence. The third objection concerns the claim that affirming the antecedent is contradictory to the implication. The answer shows that it is not contradictory; rather, the implication is already realized between them, so affirming the antecedent does not negate the implication. The exception of the negation of the consequent, however, does necessitate the negation of the antecedent. Overall, the author defends the standard theory of conditional syllogisms by clarifying the role of mental acceptance and the proper understanding of the antecedent-consequent relation.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, the productivity of a conditional syllogism depends on:
A) The factual truth of the conditional and its parts in external reality.
B) The mental acceptance of the truth of the conditional and its parts.
C) The antecedent being more general than the consequent.
D) The consequent being necessarily absent in all cases.

Key Takeaway
Conditional syllogisms are productive based on mental acceptance of the conditional, not its external truth, and objections to them can be answered by clarifying the roles of implication and the attributes of antecedent and consequent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Construct a conditional syllogism (modus ponens or modus tollens) on an Islamic topic (e.g., from fiqh or kalam) and then identify which of the three objections might be raised against it. Explain how the author's response would defend it.
?
Read the following argument: 'If this liquid is khamr, it is forbidden. This liquid is not khamr; therefore it is not forbidden.' Is this a valid conditional syllogism? Why or why not?

The Syllogism

10 min
The Nature of Malzum and Lazim in Conditional Syllogisms
Author refines the definition of malzum and lazim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the essence of the antecedent and its role as malzum (implicator) in a conditional syllogism.

Core Idea
Negating the consequent negates the antecedent only as malzum, not its essence.

In this passage, the author refines the precise meaning of malzum (antecedent) and lazim (consequent) in conditional syllogisms. He emphasizes that the antecedent is only antecedent by virtue of its implicative property, and that negating the consequent negates the antecedent in that capacity, not its essential nature. This distinction is crucial for correctly applying the modus tollens rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core principle
Locate the sentence where the author states the principle: from the negation of the consequent follows the negation of the antecedent. Notice that he specifies 'not the negation of that which has the property of being antecedent accidentally, which is the essence itself.'
2
Understand the qualification
The author explains that the antecedent is only an antecedent when qualified by the description of implying the consequent. Similarly, the consequent is only a consequent when qualified by being implied. This means the antecedent's identity as malzum is relational, not essential.
3
Apply the distinction
Consider the conditional 'If it is wine, then it is forbidden.' The malzum here is 'it is wine' in its capacity as implying forbiddenness. If we negate the consequent ('it is not forbidden'), we negate the wine's implicative capacity, not the essence of wine itself. This preserves the correctness of modus tollens.
This distinction prevents misinterpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما قد مرّ الكلام فيه أيضًا وهو أنه يلزم من انتفاء اللازم انتفاء الملزوم لا انتفاء ما يعرض له الملزومية وهو نفس الماهية من حيث هي نفس الماهية؛ فالمقدم إذن لا يكون مقدما إلا وأن يكون متصفّا بوصف كونه مستلزما للتالي، والتالي أيضًا لا يكون تاليا إلا وأن يكون متصفًا بوصف كونه لازما للمقدم. ولو كان كذلك لكان انتفاء اللازم مما يستلزم انتفاء الملزوم وهو المقدم بوصف كونه مستلزما. ولا يقال لو كان كما ذكرتم لكان الملزوم عبارة عن مجموع ذات الشيء وصفته فلا يمكن أن يكون شيئًا مفردًا البتة؛ إذ لفظ الملزوم عبارة عن شيء له الملزومية فلا يمكن أن يكون مفردًا وهو نفس ماهية الشيء لا غير. والكلام في انتفاء الملزوم بنفي اللازم لا في انتفاء تلك الماهية من حيث تلك الماهية. وإن قيل ملزومية الشيء عارضة للشيء فتكون خارجة عن ماهية الشيء وهو الملزوم. ولو كان كما ذكرتم كانت داخلة في الماهية فنقول إنها عارضة للشيء الذي هو الملزوم لا للملزوم فيكون داخلة في ماهية الملزوم لا في ماهية الشيء؛ والشيء من حيث هو الشيء لا يكون ملزوما، ولا يكون لازما بل لا يكون متصفّا بصفة أصلا . [ت] وفي الثالث نقول: إن الشيء إذا كان منافيًا للشيء لا يمكن أن يكون متصفّا به لاستحالة اتصافه بما ينافيه. وإنه يمكن أن يكون مع الصفة ولا يمكن أن يكون مع ما ينافيه البتة، ولو كان كذلك فلا يمكن أن يكون استثناء عين المقدم منافيًا للملازمة بينه وبين التالي. وكيف وإنه لا يمكن أن يكون ملزوما إلا وأن يكون الملازمة متحققة بينهما فإذن لا يمكن أن يكون منافيًا للملازمة. ولا يلزم من عدم كونه منافيًا للملازمة أن لا يكون استثناء نقيض التالي مستلزما نقيض المقدم بل يكون مستلزما وإلا لا يكون ذلك الاستثناء استثناء نقيض التالي. وأما قوله إنه إذا كان مستلزما كان استثناء عين المقدم منافيًا للملازمة بينهما لما أن نقيض المقدم من لوازم الملازمة، فذلك في حيز المنع لما أنه من لوازم الملازمة وانتفاء اللازم: وحينئذ يلزم أن يكون عين المقدم منافيًا للمجموع ولا يلزم من كون الشيء منافيا للمجموع أن يكون منافيا لكل جزء من أجزائه فلا يلزم أن يكون منافيًا للملازمة كذلك. [ث] وفي الرابع نقول : مجرد الافتراق بينهما لا يكون مانعا عن كونه منتجا وإلا لكان هذا الافتراق بينهما وهو تحقق اللازم دون تحقق الملزوم مانعا ؛ وليس كذلك فإنه إذا كان مانعا عن كونه منتجا كان مانعا عن الملازمة بينهما. وقد كان كونه منتجا من لوازم الملازمة، والمانع عن اللازم مانع عن الملزوم. وإن سلمنا كونه مانعا لكن لم قلتم بأنه لا يكون منتجا عند تحقق هذا المانع بل من اللوازم أن يكون منتجا وإلا لا يكون مستلزما على جميع التقادير وكلامنا فيما يكون مستلزما له على جميع التقادير حتى يلزم أن يكون مستلزما على تقدير أن لا يكون مستلزما كما في الإنسان مثلا فإنه إذا تحقق على تقدير أن لا يكون مستلزما للحيوان يلزم أن يكون الحيوان متحققا؛ فيكون مستلزما للحيوان على تقدير أن لا يكون مستلزما له.
What has been mentioned earlier: that from the negation of the consequent follows the negation of the antecedent, not the negation of that which has the property of being antecedent accidentally, which is the essence itself insofar as it is the essence. So the antecedent is only an antecedent by being qualified with the description of implying the consequent, and the consequent is only a consequent by being qualified with the description of being implied by the antecedent. If it were so, then the negation of the consequent would necessitate the negation of the antecedent, which is the antecedent in its capacity as implying. And it is not said: if it were as you mentioned, then the antecedent would be the combination of the thing's essence and its attribute, so it cannot be something simple at all; because the term 'antecedent' denotes a thing that has the property of being antecedent, so it cannot be simple while being the essence of the thing itself. The discussion concerns the negation of the antecedent by negating the consequent, not the negation of that essence insofar as it is that essence. And if it is said that the property of being antecedent is an accident of the thing, so it is external to the essence of the thing which is the antecedent, then if it were as you mentioned, it would be internal to the essence. So we say: it is an accident of the thing that is the antecedent, not of 'the antecedent', so it is internal to the essence of 'the antecedent', not to the essence of the thing; and the thing insofar as it is a thing is not antecedent, nor consequent, nor qualified by any attribute at all. [T] And in the third [objection] we say: If a thing is incompatible with another thing, it cannot be qualified by it because it is impossible for it to be qualified by what is incompatible with it. But it can be together with the attribute and cannot be together with what is incompatible with it at all. If it were so, then the affirmation of the antecedent cannot be incompatible with the implication between it and the consequent. And how? It cannot be antecedent unless the implication is realized between them, so it cannot be incompatible with the implication. And it does not follow from its not being incompatible with the implication that the affirmation of the opposite of the consequent is not a necessary condition for the opposite of the antecedent; rather it is a necessary condition, otherwise that affirmation would not be an affirmation of the opposite of the consequent. As for his saying that if it were a necessary condition, then the affirmation of the antecedent would be incompatible with the implication between them because the opposite of the antecedent is among the necessary consequences of the implication, that is subject to denial because it is among the necessary consequences of the implication, and the negation of the necessary consequence [leads to the negation of the implication]. And then the affirmation of the antecedent would be incompatible with the whole, and from a thing's being incompatible with the whole it does not follow that it is incompatible with each of its parts, so it does not follow that it is incompatible with the implication likewise. [Th] And in the fourth [objection] we say: mere separation between them does not prevent it from being productive, otherwise this separation between them, which is the realization of the consequent without the realization of the antecedent, would be a preventer; and it is not so because if it were a preventer from being productive, it would be a preventer of the implication between them. And its being productive is among the necessary consequences of the implication, and the preventer of the necessary consequence is a preventer of the antecedent. And if we grant that it is a preventer, why do you say that it is not productive when this preventer exists? Rather, among the necessary consequences is that it is productive, otherwise it would not be a necessary condition in all cases, and our discussion concerns what is a necessary condition in all cases, even to the extent that it would be a necessary condition on the assumption that it is not a necessary condition, as in the example of man: if he is realized on the assumption that he is not a necessary condition for animal, then animal would be realized; so he would be a necessary condition for animal on the assumption that he is not a necessary condition for it.
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement of the nature of implication in conditional syllogisms. It addresses specific objections about the relationship between the antecedent (muqaddam/malzum) and consequent (tali/lazim). The author begins by restating the fundamental principle: from the negation of the consequent follows the negation of the antecedent, but this negation does not apply to the essence of the antecedent considered in itself, but rather to the antecedent qualified by its implicative property. The antecedent is only an antecedent because it implies the consequent, and the consequent is only a consequent because it is implied by the antecedent. Consequently, negating the consequent necessitates negating the antecedent in its role as implicator. The author then addresses several objections. First, an objection that if the antecedent includes both the thing and its attribute, it cannot be simple. The author clarifies that the term 'malzum' denotes the thing with its attribute, but the discussion is about the negation of the antecedent as malzum, not the essence. Second, an objection that the property of being malzum is accidental and external to the essence; the author responds that it is accidental to the thing that is a malzum, not to 'malzum' as a concept, so it is internal to the meaning of 'malzum'. Third, a point about incompatibility: a thing cannot be qualified by what it is incompatible with, and the antecedent cannot be incompatible with the implication because the implication is essential to its being an antecedent. Therefore, affirming the antecedent does not contradict the implication. Fourth, the author argues that mere separation (realization of the consequent without the antecedent) does not prevent the syllogism from being productive; otherwise it would contradict the implication itself. The example of man and animal illustrates: man is a necessary condition for animal on all assumptions, even on the assumption that he is not a necessary condition, which demonstrates the strength of the implication.

Key Terms
الملزوم
اللازم
الملازمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, when we negate the consequent in a conditional syllogism, what exactly is negated?
A) The essence of the antecedent itself
B) The antecedent in its capacity as implying the consequent
C) The implication relation between antecedent and consequent
D) Both the antecedent and the consequent

Key Takeaway
The antecedent in a conditional syllogism is only antecedent by its implicative property; negating the consequent negates that property, not the essence.

Given the conditional 'If the act is obligatory, then it must be performed', explain what is negated when we say 'the act is not performed', according to the refined definition of malzum.

The Incompatibility Objection: Antecedent vs Implication
Author answers the third objection about incompatibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the antecedent cannot be incompatible with the implication between itself and the consequent.

Core Idea
The antecedent cannot be incompatible with the implication because being antecedent requires the implication.

In this section, the author addresses an objection that the affirmation of the antecedent might be incompatible with the implication. He argues that since the antecedent is defined by the implication, it cannot be incompatible with it. This reinforces the necessary connection between antecedent and consequent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
The objector claims that affirming the antecedent would be incompatible with the implication between it and the consequent. Find the sentence starting with 'وأما قوله...'
2
Understand the author's response
The author responds that a thing cannot be qualified by what is incompatible with it. Since the antecedent is only antecedent when the implication is realized, it cannot be incompatible with the implication.
3
Analyze the reasoning
The author argues that if the antecedent were incompatible with the implication, then the antecedent would not be antecedent at all. Therefore, affirming the antecedent does not violate the implication.
4
Apply the principle
Consider the conditional 'If it is raining, then the ground is wet.' The antecedent 'it is raining' is only meaningful as an antecedent if it implies wetness. It cannot be that 'it is raining' is true and yet the implication 'if it is raining then the ground is wet' is false. They are compatible by definition.
This shows the inseparable relation between malzum and mulazama.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما قد مرّ الكلام فيه أيضًا وهو أنه يلزم من انتفاء اللازم انتفاء الملزوم لا انتفاء ما يعرض له الملزومية وهو نفس الماهية من حيث هي نفس الماهية؛ فالمقدم إذن لا يكون مقدما إلا وأن يكون متصفّا بوصف كونه مستلزما للتالي، والتالي أيضًا لا يكون تاليا إلا وأن يكون متصفًا بوصف كونه لازما للمقدم. ولو كان كذلك لكان انتفاء اللازم مما يستلزم انتفاء الملزوم وهو المقدم بوصف كونه مستلزما. ولا يقال لو كان كما ذكرتم لكان الملزوم عبارة عن مجموع ذات الشيء وصفته فلا يمكن أن يكون شيئًا مفردًا البتة؛ إذ لفظ الملزوم عبارة عن شيء له الملزومية فلا يمكن أن يكون مفردًا وهو نفس ماهية الشيء لا غير. والكلام في انتفاء الملزوم بنفي اللازم لا في انتفاء تلك الماهية من حيث تلك الماهية. وإن قيل ملزومية الشيء عارضة للشيء فتكون خارجة عن ماهية الشيء وهو الملزوم. ولو كان كما ذكرتم كانت داخلة في الماهية فنقول إنها عارضة للشيء الذي هو الملزوم لا للملزوم فيكون داخلة في ماهية الملزوم لا في ماهية الشيء؛ والشيء من حيث هو الشيء لا يكون ملزوما، ولا يكون لازما بل لا يكون متصفّا بصفة أصلا . [ت] وفي الثالث نقول: إن الشيء إذا كان منافيًا للشيء لا يمكن أن يكون متصفّا به لاستحالة اتصافه بما ينافيه. وإنه يمكن أن يكون مع الصفة ولا يمكن أن يكون مع ما ينافيه البتة، ولو كان كذلك فلا يمكن أن يكون استثناء عين المقدم منافيًا للملازمة بينه وبين التالي. وكيف وإنه لا يمكن أن يكون ملزوما إلا وأن يكون الملازمة متحققة بينهما فإذن لا يمكن أن يكون منافيًا للملازمة. ولا يلزم من عدم كونه منافيًا للملازمة أن لا يكون استثناء نقيض التالي مستلزما نقيض المقدم بل يكون مستلزما وإلا لا يكون ذلك الاستثناء استثناء نقيض التالي. وأما قوله إنه إذا كان مستلزما كان استثناء عين المقدم منافيًا للملازمة بينهما لما أن نقيض المقدم من لوازم الملازمة، فذلك في حيز المنع لما أنه من لوازم الملازمة وانتفاء اللازم: وحينئذ يلزم أن يكون عين المقدم منافيًا للمجموع ولا يلزم من كون الشيء منافيا للمجموع أن يكون منافيا لكل جزء من أجزائه فلا يلزم أن يكون منافيًا للملازمة كذلك. [ث] وفي الرابع نقول : مجرد الافتراق بينهما لا يكون مانعا عن كونه منتجا وإلا لكان هذا الافتراق بينهما وهو تحقق اللازم دون تحقق الملزوم مانعا ؛ وليس كذلك فإنه إذا كان مانعا عن كونه منتجا كان مانعا عن الملازمة بينهما. وقد كان كونه منتجا من لوازم الملازمة، والمانع عن اللازم مانع عن الملزوم. وإن سلمنا كونه مانعا لكن لم قلتم بأنه لا يكون منتجا عند تحقق هذا المانع بل من اللوازم أن يكون منتجا وإلا لا يكون مستلزما على جميع التقادير وكلامنا فيما يكون مستلزما له على جميع التقادير حتى يلزم أن يكون مستلزما على تقدير أن لا يكون مستلزما كما في الإنسان مثلا فإنه إذا تحقق على تقدير أن لا يكون مستلزما للحيوان يلزم أن يكون الحيوان متحققا؛ فيكون مستلزما للحيوان على تقدير أن لا يكون مستلزما له.
What has been mentioned earlier: that from the negation of the consequent follows the negation of the antecedent, not the negation of that which has the property of being antecedent accidentally, which is the essence itself insofar as it is the essence. So the antecedent is only an antecedent by being qualified with the description of implying the consequent, and the consequent is only a consequent by being qualified with the description of being implied by the antecedent. If it were so, then the negation of the consequent would necessitate the negation of the antecedent, which is the antecedent in its capacity as implying. And it is not said: if it were as you mentioned, then the antecedent would be the combination of the thing's essence and its attribute, so it cannot be something simple at all; because the term 'antecedent' denotes a thing that has the property of being antecedent, so it cannot be simple while being the essence of the thing itself. The discussion concerns the negation of the antecedent by negating the consequent, not the negation of that essence insofar as it is that essence. And if it is said that the property of being antecedent is an accident of the thing, so it is external to the essence of the thing which is the antecedent, then if it were as you mentioned, it would be internal to the essence. So we say: it is an accident of the thing that is the antecedent, not of 'the antecedent', so it is internal to the essence of 'the antecedent', not to the essence of the thing; and the thing insofar as it is a thing is not antecedent, nor consequent, nor qualified by any attribute at all. [T] And in the third [objection] we say: If a thing is incompatible with another thing, it cannot be qualified by it because it is impossible for it to be qualified by what is incompatible with it. But it can be together with the attribute and cannot be together with what is incompatible with it at all. If it were so, then the affirmation of the antecedent cannot be incompatible with the implication between it and the consequent. And how? It cannot be antecedent unless the implication is realized between them, so it cannot be incompatible with the implication. And it does not follow from its not being incompatible with the implication that the affirmation of the opposite of the consequent is not a necessary condition for the opposite of the antecedent; rather it is a necessary condition, otherwise that affirmation would not be an affirmation of the opposite of the consequent. As for his saying that if it were a necessary condition, then the affirmation of the antecedent would be incompatible with the implication between them because the opposite of the antecedent is among the necessary consequences of the implication, that is subject to denial because it is among the necessary consequences of the implication, and the negation of the necessary consequence [leads to the negation of the implication]. And then the affirmation of the antecedent would be incompatible with the whole, and from a thing's being incompatible with the whole it does not follow that it is incompatible with each of its parts, so it does not follow that it is incompatible with the implication likewise. [Th] And in the fourth [objection] we say: mere separation between them does not prevent it from being productive, otherwise this separation between them, which is the realization of the consequent without the realization of the antecedent, would be a preventer; and it is not so because if it were a preventer from being productive, it would be a preventer of the implication between them. And its being productive is among the necessary consequences of the implication, and the preventer of the necessary consequence is a preventer of the antecedent. And if we grant that it is a preventer, why do you say that it is not productive when this preventer exists? Rather, among the necessary consequences is that it is productive, otherwise it would not be a necessary condition in all cases, and our discussion concerns what is a necessary condition in all cases, even to the extent that it would be a necessary condition on the assumption that it is not a necessary condition, as in the example of man: if he is realized on the assumption that he is not a necessary condition for animal, then animal would be realized; so he would be a necessary condition for animal on the assumption that he is not a necessary condition for it.
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement of the nature of implication in conditional syllogisms. It addresses specific objections about the relationship between the antecedent (muqaddam/malzum) and consequent (tali/lazim). The author begins by restating the fundamental principle: from the negation of the consequent follows the negation of the antecedent, but this negation does not apply to the essence of the antecedent considered in itself, but rather to the antecedent qualified by its implicative property. The antecedent is only an antecedent because it implies the consequent, and the consequent is only a consequent because it is implied by the antecedent. Consequently, negating the consequent necessitates negating the antecedent in its role as implicator. The author then addresses several objections. First, an objection that if the antecedent includes both the thing and its attribute, it cannot be simple. The author clarifies that the term 'malzum' denotes the thing with its attribute, but the discussion is about the negation of the antecedent as malzum, not the essence. Second, an objection that the property of being malzum is accidental and external to the essence; the author responds that it is accidental to the thing that is a malzum, not to 'malzum' as a concept, so it is internal to the meaning of 'malzum'. Third, a point about incompatibility: a thing cannot be qualified by what it is incompatible with, and the antecedent cannot be incompatible with the implication because the implication is essential to its being an antecedent. Therefore, affirming the antecedent does not contradict the implication. Fourth, the author argues that mere separation (realization of the consequent without the antecedent) does not prevent the syllogism from being productive; otherwise it would contradict the implication itself. The example of man and animal illustrates: man is a necessary condition for animal on all assumptions, even on the assumption that he is not a necessary condition, which demonstrates the strength of the implication.

اللازم
الملازمة

A) Because the antecedent is defined by the implication

C) Because the consequent is always true
D) Because the antecedent and consequent are the same

Key Takeaway
The antecedent and the implication relation are inseparable; the antecedent cannot be in conflict with its own implication.

The Separation Objection: Productivity Despite Separation
Author answers the fourth objection about separation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the mere separation of consequent from antecedent (i.e., consequent true without antecedent) does not prevent the conditional syllogism from being productive.

Core Idea
Separation does not invalidate the implication nor prevent productivity.

The fourth objection argues that if the consequent can be realized without the antecedent, then the conditional is not productive. The author responds that this separation does not prevent the syllogism from being productive, using the example of man and animal to illustrate that implication can hold even on the assumption that it does not hold.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
The objector claims that the separation between antecedent and consequent—where the consequent is true but the antecedent is false—prevents the syllogism from being productive. Find the start of the fourth objection: 'وفي الرابع نقول: مجرد الافتراق بينهما لا يكون مانعا...'
2
Understand the author's response
The author argues that if separation prevented productivity, it would also prevent the implication itself. Since the implication is necessary, separation does not affect it.
3
Follow the reductio
The author says that if separation were a preventer, it would contradict the implication because productivity is a necessary consequence of implication. He then uses the example of man and animal: man is a necessary condition for animal on all assumptions, even on the assumption that he is not a necessary condition. This demonstrates the strength of the implication.
4
Apply the principle
In a conditional like 'If it is human, then it is rational', the fact that some rational beings are not human (angels, for example) does not negate the implication. The conditional remains productive for those cases where the antecedent holds.

According to the author, does the mere separation of consequent from antecedent (i.e., consequent true without antecedent) prevent the conditional syllogism from being productive?
A) Yes, it completely invalidates the syllogism
B) No, it does not, because the implication holds even under separation
C) Yes, but only if the separation is systematic
